Cup">2013</a></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The <b>Scotland national rugby league team</b> represent <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a> in international <a href="/wiki/Rugby_league_football" class="mw-redirect" title="Rugby league football">rugby league football</a> tournaments.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> Following the break-up of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain_national_rugby_league_team" title="Great Britain national rugby league team">Great Britain</a> team in 2008,<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Scottish players play solely for Scotland, apart from occasional <a href="/wiki/Southern_Hemisphere" title="Southern Hemisphere">Southern Hemisphere</a> tours, for which the Great Britain team is expected to be revived.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> The team is nicknamed <i>the Bravehearts</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-WCOS_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WCOS-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Though its foundations may date back to as early as 1904, the team formally began in 1995,<sup id="cite_ref-WCOS_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WCOS-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> making them the newest international rugby league team in <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain" title="Great Britain">Great Britain</a>. In their first match they played <a href="/wiki/Ireland_national_rugby_league_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Ireland national rugby league team">Ireland</a>, losing narrowly. Since then, Ireland has become the team\'s main rival, the two teams having played each other many times in their short histories. In 2000 they qualified for their first ever <a href="/wiki/2000_Rugby_League_World_Cup" title="2000 Rugby League World Cup">World Cup</a>, but failed to make an impact, losing all three of their group matches;<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> however, their biggest losing margin was just 12 points.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> In 2008 they beat <a href="/wiki/Wales_national_rugby_league_team" title="Wales national rugby league team">Wales</a> over two matches to qualify for the <a href="/wiki/2008_Rugby_League_World_Cup" title="2008 Rugby League World Cup">2008 World Cup</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Scotland play in a dark blue strip, similar to the nation\'s <a href="/wiki/Scotland_national_football_team" title="Scotland national football team">football</a> and <a href="/wiki/Scotland_national_rugby_union_team" title="Scotland national rugby union team">rugby union</a> teams, with blue shirt, <a href="/wiki/Rugby_shorts" title="Rugby shorts">shorts</a> and socks. A blue and white shield with a <a href="/wiki/Onopordum_acanthium" title="Onopordum acanthium">thistle</a>, the Scottish emblem, is the team\'s badge. The shirt has rarely been significantly changed, although in the early days of the team, white was also used on the shirts.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The team is currently ranked seventh in the <a href="/wiki/RLIF_World_Rankings" title="RLIF World Rankings">RLIF World Rankings</a>, having jumped from fourth after going winless in the <a href="/wiki/2017_Rugby_League_World_Cup" title="2017 Rugby League World Cup">2017 World Cup</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> Englishman <a href="/wiki/Steve_McCormack" title="Steve McCormack">Steve McCormack</a> is the team\'s coach,<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> having coached since 2004,<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> with <a href="/wiki/Danny_Brough" title="Danny Brough">Danny Brough</a> captaining the side.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="toclimit-3"><div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span Cup</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-14"><a href="#2010s"><span class="tocnumber">1.4</span> <span class="toctext">2010s</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-3 class="toctext">2017 World Cup</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-19"><a href="#Identity"><span class="tocnumber">2</span> <span class="toctext">Identity</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-20"><a href="#Emblem"><span class="tocnumber">2.1</span> <span class="toctext">Emblem</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li tocsection-27"><a href="#Competitive_Record"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Competitive Record</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-28"><a href="#World_Cup"><span class="tocnumber">5.1</span> <span class="toctext">World Cup</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-29"><a href="#European_Cup_2"><span class="tocnumber">5.2</span> <span class="toctext">European Cup</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-30"><a href="#Four_Nations"><span class="tocnumber">5.3</span> <span class="toctext">Four Nations</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-31"><a href="#Coaches"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Coaches</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-32"><a href="#Support"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Support</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-33"><a href="#Statistics"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Statistics</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-34"><a href="#Rankings"><span class="tocnumber">8.1</span> <span class="toctext">Rankings</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-35"><a href="#Team"><span class="tocnumber">8.2</span> <span class="toctext">Team</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-36"><a href="#Other"><span class="tocnumber">8.3</span> <span class="toctext">Other</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-37"><a href="#Scotland_A"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">Scotland A</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-38"><a href="#Match_officials"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">Match officials</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-39"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-40"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-41"><a <span class="toctext">Notes</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-43"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scotland_national_rugby_league_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foundations">Foundations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scotland_national_rugby_league_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Foundations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>It could be argued that the foundations for the Scottish team began in 1904. On 5 April 1904 England played an international match against the "<a href="/wiki/Other_Nationalities_rugby_league_team" title="Other Nationalities rugby league team">Other Nationalities</a>", a team of <a href="/wiki/Welshmen" class="mw-redirect" title="Welshmen">Welshmen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Scotsmen" class="mw-redirect" title="Scotsmen">Scotsmen</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Wigan" title="Wigan">Wigan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-EVON_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EVON-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> It was a 12-a-side game. Of the twelve players who played for the Other Nationalities team two of them were Scotsmen coming from <a href="/wiki/Rugby_Football_League" title="Rugby Football League">Northern Union</a> clubs, including captain George Frater.<sup id="cite_ref-EVON_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EVON-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> After 80 minutes the Other Nationalities had beaten England 9\xe2\x80\x933.<sup id="cite_ref-EVON_14-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EVON-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> The team carried on for another two years, playing England in 1905, losing 26\xe2\x80\x9311, and in 1906, drawing 3\xe2\x80\x933.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> The team was regularly revived, most notably in the early 1930s, and in 1949.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1990s">1990s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scotland_national_rugby_league_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 1990s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Wolfhounds">The Wolfhounds</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scotland_national_rugby_league_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: The Wolfhounds">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Both Scotland and Ireland had been developing rugby league in their respective nations for several years. This was especially true at student level, with a Scotland student team having played regularly since 1987<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> and having competed in the 1992 Students World Cup.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> But it was decided that the time was right for an open-age national team to attempt to be entered into an <a href="/wiki/1995_Rugby_League_Emerging_Nations_Tournament" title="1995 Rugby League Emerging Nations Tournament">Emerging Nations Tournament</a> that would coincide with the <a href="/wiki/1995_Rugby_League_World_Cup" title="1995 Rugby League World Cup">1995 World Cup</a>, that the <a href="/wiki/Rugby_League_International_Federation" title="Rugby League International Federation">Rugby League International Federation</a> had recently announced.\n</p><p>Both <a href="/wiki/Scotland_Rugby_League" title="Scotland Rugby League">Scotland Rugby League</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rugby_League_Ireland" title="Rugby League Ireland">Rugby League Ireland</a> arranged a match on 13 August 1995 at the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Dublin_Society" title="Royal Dublin Society">Royal Dublin Showground</a> in <a href="/wiki/Dublin" title="Dublin">Dublin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ireland" title="Ireland">Ireland</a>. However the <a href="/wiki/Rugby_Football_League" title="Rugby Football League">Rugby Football League</a> provided no financial support to either team.<sup id="cite_ref-BIM_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BIM-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> Luckily the Scotland team managed to get sponsored, and the money was used for the ferry crossing, but each individual player had to pay for basic accommodation.<sup id="cite_ref-BIM_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BIM-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> The Scotland squad was largely made up of players who had played in the student squads, but a few professionals were also included.\n</p><p>Just before the start of the match, after the Scottish team had spent a night at a youth hostel, the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Rugby_Football_Union" title="Irish Rugby Football Union">Irish Rugby Football Union</a> prevented the teams from getting changed at the arranged Blackrook College.<sup id="cite_ref-DIM_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DIM-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> A new location was quickly found but it was half a mile away from the ground, and so the players had to walk that distance in their playing kit.\n</p><p>The match was looking like it would be scoreless at half-time until just before the break, centre Lee Child scored to put Ireland ahead. After the break Scotland hit back, Sean Cusack scoring Scotland\'s first ever try. Gavin Manclark then scored to propel Scotland into the lead. This did not last long though, as Leo Casey scored for Ireland in the 55th minute. Ireland then scored again, with Seamus McCallion going over. Four minutes later in the 69th minute, Scotland quickly scored two tries with Manclark and Shelford sealing the eight points. However, this was not enough as Ketteridge had only kicked three conversions compared to Ireland\'s Ian Devery who had kicked five. The match finished with Ireland winning 26\xe2\x80\x9322, but Thompson for Scotland did win Man of the Match.<sup id="cite_ref-DIM_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DIM-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="1995_Emerging_Nations_tournament">1995 Emerging Nations tournament</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scotland_national_rugby_league_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 1995 Emerging Nations tournament">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>After this international Scotland were allowed to take place in the <a href="/wiki/1995_Rugby_League_Emerging_Nations_Tournament" title="1995 Rugby League Emerging Nations Tournament">Emerging Nations Tournament</a>, which was to be held in <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a>. On 16 October 1995 at <a href="/wiki/Featherstone" title="Featherstone">Featherstone</a> they faced <a href="/wiki/Russia_national_rugby_league_team" title="Russia national rugby league team">Russia</a>, who had been playing international rugby league since 1991, in their opening game in Group A. Coached by former <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain_national_rugby_league_team" title="Great Britain national rugby league team">Great Britain</a> and England (despite the fact he was Scottish) player, <a href="/wiki/George_Fairbairn_(rugby_league)" title="George Fairbairn (rugby league)">George Fairbairn</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> who put together a team of former Scotland students, <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">rugby union</a> players, and a few league professionals including <a href="/wiki/Alan_Tait" title="Alan Tait">Alan Tait</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> who played for <a href="/wiki/Leeds_Rhinos" title="Leeds Rhinos">Leeds</a>, and who would captain the side.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> The whole of the Scotland team had hired <a href="/wiki/Kilts" class="mw-redirect" title="Kilts">kilts</a> to be worn pre-match.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The game started off well for Scotland, student James How scoring after just four minutes.<sup id="cite_ref-RUS_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RUS-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> And then minutes later Tait doubled the Bravehearts lead.<sup id="cite_ref-RUS_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RUS-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> But the Russia Bears dragged themselves back into the match, stand-off Victor Netchaev scoring first, and in the 30th minute Alexander Otradnov scored.<sup id="cite_ref-RUS_26-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RUS-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> Scotland were ahead though at half-time by four points because Russia had failed to convert their tries.<sup id="cite_ref-RUS_26-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RUS-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> In the second half it was all Scotland with only Andrey Scheglov\'s drop goal adding to the Bears points.<sup id="cite_ref-RUS_26-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RUS-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> On the other hand, former Great Britain international Hugh Waddell, Ali Blee and Tait again all scored to seal a Scottish victory.<sup id="cite_ref-ENT_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ENT-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable" style="text-align:center; float:right;">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<td><b>Group One Table</b></td>\n<td><b>W</b></td>\n<td><b>L</b></td>\n<td><b>F</b></td>\n<td><b>A</b></td>\n<td><b>PTS</b>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Cook_Islands_national_rugby_league_team" title="Cook Islands national rugby league team">Cook Islands</a></td>\n<td>3</td>\n<td>0</td>\n<td>143</td>\n<td>36</td>\n<td>6\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:turquoise;">\n<td><b>Scotland</b></td>\n<td style="background:turquoise;"><b>2</b></td>\n<td style="background:turquoise;"><b>1</b></td>\n<td style="background:turquoise;"><b>82</b></td>\n<td style="background:turquoise;"><b>46</b></td>\n<td style="background:turquoise;"><b>4</b>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Russia_national_rugby_league_team" title="Russia national rugby league team">Russia</a></td>\n<td>1</td>\n<td>2</td>\n<td>57</td>\n<td>118</td>\n<td>2\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/United_States_national_rugby_league_team" title="United States national rugby league team">United States</a></td>\n<td>0</td>\n<td>3</td>\n<td>48</td>\n<td>130</td>\n<td>0\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Scotland\'s second match was against the <a href="/wiki/United_States_national_rugby_league_team" title="United States national rugby league team">United States</a> in <a href="/wiki/Northampton" title="Northampton">Northampton</a>, traditionally a <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">rugby union</a> city.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> The Tomahawks were made up of <a href="/wiki/AMNRL" class="mw-redirect" title="AMNRL">AMNRL</a> players but Scotland took a while to get going. In the twelfth minute winger Rory Lewis unexpected put America ahead, which caused The Bravehearts to start playing well for the remainder of the first half, Scotland eventually going into the second half leading three tries to one. Graeme Thompson had kicked a penalty very early on in the game, and then after the America try added another four points. McAlister, who had missed the conversion, set up Ketteridge and Smith for Scotland\'s second and third tries respectively. The Bravehearts extended their lead in the second half, Shelford going over and then David Niu, who could have played for Scotland because of his <a href="/wiki/Dunfermline" title="Dunfermline">Dunfermline</a> born mother, got one back for the States. But Scotland put a victory beyond doubt with Alan Tait setting up Shelford twice for his hat-trick. Late in the game Niu and Steve Tait scored for the United States and Scotland respectively to end the match 38\xe2\x80\x9316 in Scotland\'s favour.<sup id="cite_ref-ENT_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ENT-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Scotland\'s two victories, coupled with the <a href="/wiki/Cook_Islands_national_rugby_league_team" title="Cook Islands national rugby league team">Cook Islands</a> ability to beat the United States and Russia too,<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> set up a deciding match in\n<a href="/wiki/Castleford" title="Castleford">Castleford</a> where the winner would reach the final. 3,000 people turned up to first see Thompson score a penalty after 15 minutes, but then Nigere Tariu slid over to put the Islanders ahead. Just before the break however, Tait charged through three players to put Scotland back in the game. In the second half the Cook Islands, with several <a href="/wiki/NRL" class="mw-redirect" title="NRL">NRL</a> players in their ranks, showed their strength as Sonny Shepherd scored a controversial try as Scottish players complained about the grounding. From a play the ball Shepherd went over again and in the 73rd minute Tariu scored a converted try. The Bravehearts did get a late consolation, skipper Tait going over for Scotland\'s last try before Islander Ali Davys sealed Scotland\'s fate with a drop-goal. The match finished Scotland 10\xe2\x80\x9321 Cook Islands.<sup id="cite_ref-ENT_27-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ENT-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> In the final the Cook Islands beat Ireland 22\xe2\x80\x936 in <a href="/wiki/Bury,_Greater_Manchester" title="Bury, Greater Manchester">Bury</a> to win the tournament and secure a place in the next World Cup.<sup id="cite_ref-ENT_27-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ENT-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> Despite losing this final match the Scotland team and supporters thought that they had done very well considering how young the team was and how well their performances had been against Russia and the USA.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Glasgow_matches">Glasgow matches</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scotland_national_rugby_league_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Glasgow matches">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>In 1996 the <a href="/wiki/Rugby_League_International_Federation" title="Rugby League International Federation">Rugby League International Federation</a> rewarded Scotland with full international status<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> which meant that they could start organising more fixtures and there was no longer a limit to the number of professionals they could use.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> Before this status Scotland had been restricted to playing just three professionals in a match.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="toccolours" style="background:#cedff2; width:30%; float:left; margin-right:1em;">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td><div class="quotebox pullquote" style="; background-color: #cedff2; border:0;margin:0;"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303512">.mw-parser-output .quotebox{background-color:#F9F9F9;border:1px solid #aaa;box-sizing:border-box;padding:10px;font-size:88%}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft{margin:0.5em 1.4em 0.8em 0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright{margin:0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.centered{margin:0.5em auto 0.8em auto}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft p,.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright p{font-style:inherit}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-title{background-color:#F9F9F9;text-align:center;font-size:larger;font-weight:bold}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:before{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" \xe2\x80\x9c ";vertical-align:-45%;line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:after{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" \xe2\x80\x9d ";line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .left-aligned{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .right-aligned{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .center-aligned{text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .quotebox cite{display:block;font-style:normal}@media screen and (max-width:360px){.mw-parser-output .quotebox{min-width:100%;margin:0 0 0.8em!important;float:none!important}}</style>\n<div class="quotebox-quote left-aligned" style="">Referee Blows Time On Scots\' History Hopes</div>\n<p><cite class="right-aligned" style="">\xe2\x80\x94 <i><a href="/wiki/Daily_Mail" title="Daily Mail">Daily Mail</a></i> headline.<sup id="cite_ref-SAM_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SAM-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup></cite>\n</p>\n</div><div class="quotebox pullquote" style="; background-color: #cedff2; border:0;margin:0;"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303512"/>\n<div class="quotebox-quote left-aligned" style="">Scots In Rage At Bungling Whistler</div>\n<p><cite class="right-aligned" style="">\xe2\x80\x94 <i><a href="/wiki/The_Sun_(United_Kingdom)" title="The Sun (United Kingdom)">The Sun</a></i> headline.<sup id="cite_ref-SAM_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SAM-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup></cite>\n</p>\n</div><div class="quotebox pullquote" style="; background-color: #cedff2; border:0;margin:0;"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303512"/>\n<div class="quotebox-quote left-aligned" style="">The guys are all gutted about it and I am gutted for them. They had come back so well after a mediocre first half.</div>\n<p><cite class="right-aligned" style="">\xe2\x80\x94 Coach <a href="/wiki/George_Fairbairn_(rugby_league)" title="George Fairbairn (rugby league)">George Fairbairn</a> after the match.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup></cite>\n</p>\n</div><div class="quotebox pullquote" style="; background-color: #cedff2; border:0;margin:0;"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303512"/>\n<div class="quotebox-quote left-aligned" style="">An obvious error took place which changed the outcome of the game. The touch judge clearly indicated an infringement, but in a moment of excitement, the referee decided to go with his own instincts. The guy\'s distraught about it and realises that he has made a mistake</div>\n<p><cite class="right-aligned" style="">\xe2\x80\x94 Referees\' director Greg McCallum.<sup id="cite_ref-SAM_35-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SAM-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup></cite>\n</p>\n</div>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Scotland faced Ireland again in August of that year, and it was to be their first home game, with the match being played at the <a href="/wiki/Firhill_Stadium" title="Firhill Stadium">Firhill Stadium</a> in Glasgow. After 5 minutes Alan Tait touched down with Matt Crowther converting. And then hooker Danny Russell and professional Darren Shaw gave the Bravehearts a 14\xe2\x80\x930 lead at half-time. In the second half after 52 minutes Lee Hanlon scored Ireland\'s only try of the match, but Martin Ketteridge soon kicked a penalty for Scotland to extend the lead. In the closing stages of the match, after three Irish players had been sin-binned, Darrall Shaleford and Nick Mardon got themselves on the scoreboard with a try each. The match finished Scotland 26\xe2\x80\x936 Ireland.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> This is the only time in eight attempts that Scotland have beaten Ireland.\n</p><p>A second match in Glasgow was held in July 1997 against <a href="/wiki/France_national_rugby_league_team" title="France national rugby league team">France</a>. The match was to end in controversy surrounding a late try and French referee Thierry Alibert. France had got off to a good start, with Freddie Banquet scoring before Danny Russell and Gary Christie scored a try each to send the Scots in front. However, with a few minutes to go before half-time, <a href="/wiki/Jerome_Guisset" class="mw-redirect" title="Jerome Guisset">Jerome Guisset</a> scored under the posts to give the French side a 12\xe2\x80\x9310 lead after 40 minutes. After half-time France extended their lead through Fabien Devecchi but once again Scotland rallied together and Stuart McCarthy scored a crucial try, which was not converted. In the 70th minute Matt Crowther scored a try, and converted it, to put Scotland into a 20\xe2\x80\x9318 lead. With just seconds remaining, a storm brewed when referee Alibert awarded a try to France\'s Arnauld Dulac. The Bravehearts and coaching staff said that the ball was knocked on, and therefore a scrum should have occurred.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> English touch judge Peter Walton signalled the knock-on but play continued. The match finished Scotland 20\xe2\x80\x9322 France.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Clash_of_the_Nations">Clash of the Nations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scotland_national_rugby_league_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Clash of the Nations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The Clash of the Nations was a new tournament designed to make November 1998 a month of international league as Great Britain was touring the Southern Hemisphere. Scotland, France and Ireland would play two matches each and the winner of the two matches would be crowned champion.\n</p><p>Scotland first faced France in Perpignan, the first match since they were controversially denied a victory in 1996. New coach <a href="/wiki/Billy_McGinty_(rugby_league)" title="Billy McGinty (rugby league)">Billy McGinty</a> promised "the strongest ever Scotland squad" and just three players survived from Scotland\'s last international match.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> D\xc3\xa9butant <a href="/wiki/Jason_Flowers" title="Jason Flowers">Jason Flowers</a> put Scotland ahead, before France levelled the scores. But <a href="/wiki/Danny_Arnold_(rugby_league)" title="Danny Arnold (rugby league)">Danny Arnold</a> once again put the Bravehearts ahead. Scotland excelled and <a href="/wiki/Jason_Roach_(rugby_league)" title="Jason Roach (rugby league)">Jason Roach</a> further strengthened Scotland\'s lead before France narrowed the lead to four points at half-time. In the 55th minute France scored to take the lead for the first time in the match. Roach got his second try, but France retaliated by scoring one of their own. Ten minutes from full-time France scored another try to confirm the two points.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> The match finished France 26\xe2\x80\x9322 Scotland, with <a href="/wiki/Lee_Penny" title="Lee Penny">Lee Penny</a> earning Man of the Match award.\n</p><p>France went onto beat Ireland in their second match, therefore clinching the trophy, however Scotland still played Ireland in Glasgow, the first meeting between these nations since 1995. The first half was to prove uneventful, with Ireland scoring a single try to make the score 6\xe2\x80\x930 after 40 minutes. On the 46th minute Ireland drifted into a 10-point lead, but <a href="/wiki/John_Duffy_(rugby_league)" title="John Duffy (rugby league)">John Duffy</a> kept the Bravehearts in the match with 20 minutes of the match remaining. <a href="/wiki/Logan_Campbell_(rugby_league)" title="Logan Campbell (rugby league)">Logan Campbell</a> got a try for Scotland but then Ireland scored another, a drop-goal to win the match 17\xe2\x80\x9310. <a href="/wiki/Colin_Wilson_(rugby_league)" title="Colin Wilson (rugby league)">Colin Wilson</a> was awarded the Man of the Match award, and significantly became the first player from the Scottish Conference domestic league to represent Scotland.\n</p><p>With two defeats from the tournament Scotland finished bottom of the table.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Triangular_Challenge">Triangular Challenge</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scotland_national_rugby_league_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Triangular Challenge">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>England have competed in 26 European Nations Cups, the first in 1935. In the past the tournament has been axed and revived many times, and it was stopped for six years because of the Second World War. From 1935 to 1949 (minus the war years) England played France and Wales annually, and won the tournament in 1935, 1946, 1947 and 1948. From 1950 to 1956 an Other Nationalities team were added as the fourth team in the competition (except in 1956 when Wales did not field a team). During those years England won in 1950 and 1954. Since then the tournament has run for some seasons, but never for more than five years at a time. But from 1970 to 1996 England won it six out of a possible nine times. In 2003 the tournament was revived and England comfortably won, beating her old rivals plus Scotland, Ireland and Russia. England beat the same opponents to win the cup again in 2004. This was the last time England competed, they were replaced by Georgia. The cup ran for just one more year before it was axed again. It has not since returned. In total England have won the cup fourteen times.\n</p><p>With The Clash of the Nations tournament over, the Celtic nations were to play each other once over October and November in a new competition. The matches were to coincide with the Great Britain versus Australia matches, in which Great Britain ended up being badly beaten. Dale Laughton was the only Scotman in the Great Britain team and so the Bravehearts didn\'t suffer from withdrawals as much as Ireland and Wales did.<sup id="cite_ref-TCT_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TCT-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> It is generally regarded that the Rugby Football League made the same mistakes as the 1998 tournament with matches being held on Friday nights and competing against both the football and rugby union seasons and consequently attendances were very low for the matches.<sup id="cite_ref-TCT_43-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TCT-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> The first of Scotland\'s matches was against Wales in which many of the best Welsh players were with Great Britain. Scotland took the lead through Danny Arnold but The Dragons quickly made the game level. Captain Danny Russell went over for Scotland\'s second try, but once again Wales hit back within minutes. Andrew Lambert scored just before half-time for The Bravehearts but the lead did not last long after the break with Wales scoring. However, the Welsh were unable to reply to the next four tries, with Mike Wainwright and Matt Crowther each getting themselves onto the scoreboard and both Lambert and Arnold getting their second tries.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> A win or a draw would seal Scotland\'s place at the top of the table but Ireland mixture of Super League and local players were too good for Scotland. They raced into a 1ten point lead before Russell and Arnold, with Crowther converting one, allowed Scotland to claw their way back into the match. In the final quarter the Bravehearts fell apart, leaking in 21 points to lose the match.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2000s">2000s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scotland_national_rugby_league_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: 2000s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2000_World_Cup">2000 World Cup</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scotland_national_rugby_league_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: 2000 World Cup">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2000_Rugby_League_World_Cup" title="2000 Rugby League World Cup">2000 Rugby League World Cup</a></div>\n<p>Scotland were placed in Group 4 in the 16-team Rugby League World Cup for 2000, which was held in the United Kingdom and France.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> This meant that they would face Ireland, Samoa and New Zealand Maori, with one match being played at <a href="/wiki/Glasgow" title="Glasgow">Glasgow</a>, and one match being played in <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh" title="Edinburgh">Edinburgh</a>. Out of the four teams, two would then qualify for the Quarter Finals, playing the top teams from other groups.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> The Scots World Cup campaign was criticised though, before the tournament was even started when the 24-man squad was named, as not one of the players were born in Scotland.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In their first match after the World Cup campaign, Scotland faced France in the southern French town of <a href="/wiki/Lezignan-Corbieres" class="mw-redirect" title="Lezignan-Corbieres">Lezignan</a>. Shaun McRae, citing his domestic coaching at <a href="/wiki/Hull_F.C." title="Hull F.C.">Hull</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> departed as Scotland coach and Glasgow-born Billy McGinty took over the role with the then <a href="/wiki/Swinton_Lions" title="Swinton Lions">Swinton Lions</a> coach and former Great Britain player <a href="/wiki/Mike_Gregory" title="Mike Gregory">Mike Gregory</a> taking the role of assistant coach.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> The squad for this match included 13 survivors from the World Cup matches and three new players who were each earning their first international cap.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> The Scots got off to a great start, scoring three tries in the first 13 minutes and never looked back as they won the match 42\xe2\x80\x9320.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> The heat in the French summer was thought to be a problem going into the match, but Scotland scored seven tries in total to record their first win against the French and arguably their best win yet in international competition.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> Two tries each were scored by Danny Arnold and Jason Flowers, and Matt Crowther converted all seven tries. Seven years later this victory is Scotland\'s biggest win and is still recognised as one of their best amongst supporters.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="European_Cup">European Cup</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scotland_national_rugby_league_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: European Cup">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Scotland joined the prestigious European Nations Cup tournament in 2003, now being regarded as the seventh best national nation.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> This newly expanded competition, which also featured Russia and Ireland for the first time,<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> as well as England A, France and Wales, was split into two groups with the winner of each group playing each other to become the competition\'s champions. Scotland were placed in a group with rivals Ireland and France. In May 2003, several months before the start of the tournament, Scotland Rugby League announced that <a href="/wiki/Mike_Gregory" title="Mike Gregory">Mike Gregory</a> would become the new coach of the Scottish team, with <a href="/wiki/David_Lyon_(rugby_league)" title="David Lyon (rugby league)">David Lyon</a> being appointed as his assistant.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> However it was later announced that due to Mike Gregorys commitments to <a href="/wiki/Wigan_Warriors" title="Wigan Warriors">Wigan Warriors</a>, McGinty will continue to coach the side.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> Scotland\'s first match was against Ireland at <a href="/wiki/Old_Anniesland" title="Old Anniesland">Old Anniesland</a>. The Scots lost by just two points, with <a href="/wiki/Lee_Penny" title="Lee Penny">Lee Penny</a>, <a href="/wiki/Danny_Arnold_(rugby_league)" title="Danny Arnold (rugby league)">Danny Arnold</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jason_Roach_(rugby_league)" title="Jason Roach (rugby league)">Jason Roach</a> all scoring tries for Scotland, but <a href="/wiki/John_Duffy_(rugby_league)" title="John Duffy (rugby league)">John Duffy</a> had missed one of his crucial four goals.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> Scotland were 12\xe2\x80\x932 up after 21 minutes and were level at half-time, but Irish substitute <a href="/wiki/Karl_Fitzpatrick" title="Karl Fitzpatrick">Karl Fitzpatrick</a> gave the Wolfhounds the win in the last few minutes of the match.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> With France then beating Ireland in Dublin, Scotland now knew that they could clinch first place. The match held in Narbonne, between France and Scotland turned out to be closely fought. However, the Scots came out on top with an <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Henderson_(rugby_league)" title="Andrew Henderson (rugby league)">Andrew Henderson</a> try and two <a href="/wiki/Oliver_Wilkes" title="Oliver Wilkes">Oliver Wilkes</a> goals sealing the victory by two points.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> This scoreline meant that all three teams had finished on two points, but it was France, with the better points difference, that went on to face England in the final.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The 2004 competition followed the same plan but this time the Bravehearts were with Ireland and Wales. These two teams had already played each other a week earlier with the result and Irish victory.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> Both sides scored four tries, but it was the kicking of Danny Brough that helped Scotland to beat the Dragons by 30 points to 22 in Glasgow.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> The match drew over a thousand spectators and was the first time Scotland had won at home for five years.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> Just five days later though, the team had to play their second game against the Irish Wolfhounds in Ireland. Despite a try from Spencer Miller and three successful kicks by Danny Brough, the Irish ran out easy winners with the match ending 43\xe2\x80\x9310 and thus ending Scotlands campaign in the cup.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2008_World_Cup_Qualifying">2008 World Cup Qualifying</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scotland_national_rugby_league_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: 2008 World Cup Qualifying">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2008_Rugby_League_World_Cup_qualifying" title="2008 Rugby League World Cup qualifying">2008 Rugby League World Cup qualifying</a></div>\n<p>On 17 May 2006 Scotland received word that they would play two matches against Wales for a place in the 2008 World Cup.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> The two matches of Group 1 (there were two European groups) would be contested in late 2006 and 2007, with the first being in Bridgend and the second being in Glasgow.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Before the first match, coach Steve McCormack had time with the players in training camps in Huddersfield and Swansea, and admitted that he was not threatened by the likes of Super League giants <a href="/wiki/Iestyn_Harris" title="Iestyn Harris">Iestyn Harris</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lee_Briers" title="Lee Briers">Lee Briers</a> in the Welsh team.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> This is despite many fans and journalists favouring the Dragons to easily win.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> McCormack later named his squad for the match, which included a mixture of Super League, National League and Rugby League Conference players.<sup id="cite_ref-FWS_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FWS-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> Five of them would be making their d\xc3\xa9but, but long-serving player <a href="/wiki/Ian_Henderson_(rugby_league)" title="Ian Henderson (rugby league)">Ian Henderson</a>, who had played in every Scottish match since 2001, was unable to play for in this match.<sup id="cite_ref-FWS_73-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FWS-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Scotland started well in Bridgend with Wade Liddell giving the Bravehearts the lead after just 8 minutes. This try was converted by Gareth Morton. But things got bad as Wales pulled a try back through Richard Johnson, and then Danny Brough was sinbinned for dissent on 26 minutes. In the next ten minutes a Wales team minus Iestyn Harris, who failed a fitness test prior to the match,<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> capitalised on Scotland\'s shortfall and scored two tries to create a 14\xe2\x80\x936 lead going into half-time.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> However, after the break the Scots immediately got back into the match, Danny Brough singlehandedly scoring a try after 70 seconds of the interval, and Jamie Benn a little later leeching on to a grubber kick. Mick Nanyn missed both conversions and so the scores were tied. On the 67th minute Scotland went in front, Nanyn converting his own try. And to seal a 21\xe2\x80\x9314 victory Danny Brough scored a drop-goal.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> He would later get Man of the Match award.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>To prepare for the second qualification match, Scotland travelled to Perpignan to play test nation France. Scotland rested several key players, like Danny Brough and Ian Henderson,<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> and gave caps to six d\xc3\xa9but players.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> It turned out to be a bad decision as Scotland suffered their heaviest defeat in their history. After 15 minutes Scotland were trailing 18\xe2\x80\x930,<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> and despite tries from Benn, Nanyn and Paterson, plus two successful conversions from Nanyn, France were always well ahead. The match finished France 46\xe2\x80\x9316 Scotland.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Before the second qualification match in Glasgow, Wales were still confident of victory with the Dragons assistant coach Kevin Ellis saying that his Welsh team had some fantastic players, and that it was the best since Wales golden era of 1991\xe2\x80\x931995.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> But Scotland had the advantage going into the match, for a win or draw or even a small loss would guarantee them a place in the cup. Before the match Danny Brough was announced as captain before the match, thus earning his sixth cap too.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the first half of the match Wales were on top, with Scotland only managing to score four points overall, two penalties by Danny Brough. Richard Fletcher had been carried off after an aerial collision, which caused the game to be stopped for six minutes.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> At half time the score was 14\xe2\x80\x934 in favour of the Dragons, meaning Scotland would not qualify.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> In the 52nd minute Ben Fisher darted over the line to score Scotland\'s first try. Importantly this was converted by Danny Brough.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> And with seven minutes remaining Jamie Benn latched onto Mick Nanyn\'s speculative pass to score Scotland\'s second try,<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> which Brough converted. Wales scored late on but it was not enough. The match finished Scotland 16\xe2\x80\x9318 Wales,<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> with an aggregate score of Scotland 37\xe2\x80\x9332,<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> and Mick Nanyn received Man of the Match award.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2008_World_Cup">2008 World Cup</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scotland_national_rugby_league_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: 2008 World Cup">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>On 9 July 2008, Scotland Rugby League announced that Steve McCormack had signed a 12-month deal to continue his job as head coach of the Scotland team.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> Danny Brough will continue to skipper the team into the World Cup, providing he stays fit.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> Except for <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh_Eagles" title="Edinburgh Eagles">Edinburgh Eagles</a> stand-off <a href="/wiki/Paddy_Couper" class="mw-redirect" title="Paddy Couper">Paddy Couper</a>, all of the Scottish team\'s players were selected under the <a href="/wiki/Grandparent_rule" class="mw-redirect" title="Grandparent rule">grandparent rule</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> \nIn the group stage they made history as they finally won a game and it was against <a href="/wiki/Fiji_national_rugby_league_team" title="Fiji national rugby league team">Fiji</a> who were demolishing opponents courtesy of superstars such as <a href="/wiki/Jarryd_Hayne" title="Jarryd Hayne">Jarryd Hayne</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>  But that is as far as they finished in the <a href="/wiki/2008_Rugby_League_World_Cup" title="2008 Rugby League World Cup">2008 Rugby League World Cup</a> because their points differential was worse than Fiji\'s and <a href="/wiki/France_national_rugby_league_team" title="France national rugby league team">France</a> who were also in their group and were demolished by them in their first game of the 2008 campaign. Several NRL and Super League stars were in McCormack\'s team for the tournament including <a href="/wiki/Manly-Warringah_Sea_Eagles" class="mw-redirect" title="Manly-Warringah Sea Eagles">Manly-Warringah Sea Eagles</a> winger/fullback <a href="/wiki/Michael_Robertson_(rugby_league)" title="Michael Robertson (rugby league)">Michael Robertson</a> who had scored 3 tries in Manly\'s 40\xe2\x80\x930 triumph over the <a href="/wiki/Melbourne_Storm" title="Melbourne Storm">Melbourne Storm</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2008_NRL_Grand_Final" title="2008 NRL Grand Final">2008 NRL Grand Final</a> just prior to the tournament as well as crossing for 18 tries in the <a href="/wiki/2008_NRL_season" title="2008 NRL season">2008 NRL season</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2010s">2010s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scotland_national_rugby_league_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: 2010s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2013_World_Cup">2013 World Cup</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scotland_national_rugby_league_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: 2013 World Cup">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>No Qualification was required for the Bravehearts for the <a href="/wiki/2013_Rugby_League_World_Cup" title="2013 Rugby League World Cup">2013 Rugby League World Cup</a> due to participating in the 2008 tournament. They were drawn in pool C alongside World Cup debutantes <a href="/wiki/Italy_national_rugby_league_team" title="Italy national rugby league team">Italy</a> and the powerful forwards and fast backs of <a href="/wiki/Tonga_national_rugby_league_team" title="Tonga national rugby league team">Tonga</a>. Every team needed to play 3 group games each so Scotland would also play an inter-group game against the other World Cup debutantes the <a href="/wiki/United_States_national_rugby_league_team" title="United States national rugby league team">United States</a>. The Scots were underdogs against the Pacific Island nation who were full of NRL talent. But Scotland, in front of a record crowd at <a href="/wiki/Derwent_Park" title="Derwent Park">Derwent Park</a> made another upset (like Fiji five years ago) winning a tough match by only a two-point margin at the end of the match. Scotland\'s second match was against the Italians at the same venue in front of more than 7,000 fans again who this time witnessed a high scoring draw. Scotland then finished their group stage by beating the United States convincingly. Scotland had almost qualified for the World Cup knockout stage for the first ever time but Italy were still within a chance to finish above Scotland and therefore eliminate Scotland\'s chances from progressing any further in the 2013 tournament. Italy only needed to win after they were also on 16+ points differential and they were facing Tonga who had absolutely nothing at stake but pride to play for. But, a shock to all, Tonga outclassed the Italians and eliminated them from participating any further in the competition. In the quarter-final they had a rare clash with a rugby league heavyweight. They took on <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand_national_rugby_league_team" title="New Zealand national rugby league team">New Zealand</a> in Leeds in front of their biggest attendance away from Scotland. Despite their early defensive pressure that the crowd loved to cheer out loud for, Scotland\'s lack of experience against the heavyweight nations showed on the scoreboard and were therefore eliminated in a pleasing World Cup performance.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2010s_European_Cup">2010s European Cup</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scotland_national_rugby_league_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: 2010s European Cup">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>In 2010 the <a href="/wiki/Rugby_League_European_Cup#League_Leaders_(2010\xe2\x80\x93Onwards)" class="mw-redirect" title="Rugby League European Cup">European Cup</a> reverted to the \'League Leaders\' being the winners rather than having final games like the 2000s decade. In the <a href="/wiki/2010_European_Cup" title="2010 European Cup">2010 European Cup</a> and <a href="/wiki/2012_European_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="2012 European Cup">2012 European Cup</a> competitions Scotland only managed to finish third in each tournament recording with only one total victory.\n</p><p>In October and November 2014, 2013 Super League <a href="/wiki/Man_of_Steel_Awards" title="Man of Steel Awards">Man of Steel Award</a> winner and <a href="/wiki/RLIF_Awards#International_Player_of_the_Year" title="RLIF Awards">RLIF International Player of the Year</a> shortlist award finalist <a href="/wiki/Danny_Brough" title="Danny Brough">Danny Brough</a> led Scotland in the <a href="/wiki/2014_European_Cup_(rugby_league)" class="mw-redirect" title="2014 European Cup (rugby league)">2014 European Cup</a>. He shared his belief saying that Scotland have the quality and deserve playing at a higher International level after the 2013 Rugby League World Cup performance.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> The Winner of the tournament would qualify to play in the <a href="/wiki/2016_Rugby_League_Four_Nations" title="2016 Rugby League Four Nations">2016 Four Nations</a> alongside International heavyweights Australia, England and New Zealand. Brough played at his best throughout the tournament, earning him the \'Player of the Tournament\' award.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> His performances and leadership inspired and influenced the team to qualify for 2016\'s major international rugby league competition.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2016_Four_Nations">2016 Four Nations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scotland_national_rugby_league_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: 2016 Four Nations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Scotland qualified for the 2016 Four Nations series and would be co hosts with England.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2017_World_Cup">2017 World Cup</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scotland_national_rugby_league_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: 2017 World Cup">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>After making the finals of the 2013 tournament, Scotland automatically qualified for the <a href="/wiki/2017_Rugby_League_World_Cup" title="2017 Rugby League World Cup">2017 Rugby League World Cup</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Identity">Identity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scotland_national_rugby_league_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Identity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Scotjumper.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Scotjumper.jpg/150px-Scotjumper.jpg" width="150" height="130" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Scotjumper.jpg/225px-Scotjumper.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Scotjumper.jpg/300px-Scotjumper.jpg 2x" data-file-width="392" data-file-height="340" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Scotjumper.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>This shirt was used for the two World Cup Qualifying matches against Wales.</div></div></div>\n<p>Since their first match Scotland have always played in royal blue, with a royal blue shirt, shorts and socks. In their two World Cup qualifying matches in 2007, the Scottish flag, featuring the white cross on a blue background, was on each shoulder and also on the shirt was a white collar.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> On the left of the shirt is the Scotland badge, and on the right is the Great Britain badge which is split into four and then has the England, Scotland, Wales and Ireland rugby league badges in a shield.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> This is to signify Scotland\'s part in the Great Britain setup.\n</p><p>In early 2008 Scotland Rugby League announced that they had secured a five-figure sponsorship deal with <a href="/wiki/The_Co-operative_brand" title="The Co-operative brand">The Co-operative</a> which would see the world\'s largest consumer-owned businesses logo on the front of the shirts for the 2008 World Cup and for all 2009 matches too.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cirsium_vulgare_flowers_Anstey_Hill.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Cirsium_vulgare_flowers_Anstey_Hill.jpg/150px-Cirsium_vulgare_flowers_Anstey_Hill.jpg" width="150" height="113" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Cirsium_vulgare_flowers_Anstey_Hill.jpg/225px-Cirsium_vulgare_flowers_Anstey_Hill.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Cirsium_vulgare_flowers_Anstey_Hill.jpg/300px-Cirsium_vulgare_flowers_Anstey_Hill.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cirsium_vulgare_flowers_Anstey_Hill.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Scotch thistle, open and closed.</div></div></div>\n<p>A new shirt has recently been designed for the World Cup and it is expected that fans will be able to buy it\nsometime in the Summer 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> Instead of the Great Britain badge on the right, there will be the World Cup logo, similar to each of the ten teams shirts. The shirt is made by German sportswear company <a href="/wiki/Puma_AG" class="mw-redirect" title="Puma AG">Puma</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Scotland\'s current kit suppliers are <a href="/wiki/Beyond_Limits_Known" class="mw-redirect" title="Beyond Limits Known">BLK</a>. On the shirt, <a href="/wiki/Bartercard" title="Bartercard">Bartercard</a> is on the front (replacing <a href="/wiki/Highland_Spring" title="Highland Spring">Highland Spring</a> as of 2017) while Match Point is on the right sleeve while on the back, <a href="/wiki/Caledonian_Brewery" title="Caledonian Brewery">Caledonian Brewery</a> is on the top while <a href="/wiki/Lucozade_Sport" class="mw-redirect" title="Lucozade Sport">Lucozade Sport</a> is on the bottom.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Emblem">Emblem</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scotland_national_rugby_league_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Emblem">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The emblem of the Scotland team is the thistle, which is on the team\'s badge in a crest.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> The thistle is an ancient Celtic symbol of nobility of character as well as of birth and is the symbol of the <a href="/wiki/Order_of_the_Thistle" title="Order of the Thistle">Order of the Thistle</a> a high <a href="/wiki/Chivalric_order" class="mw-redirect" title="Chivalric order">chivalric order</a> of Scotland.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> There is also a well-known Scottish legend that in <a href="/wiki/Medieval" class="mw-redirect" title="Medieval">Medieval</a> times a <a href="/wiki/Viking" class="mw-redirect" title="Viking">Viking</a>, wanting to invade Scotland, stood on a thistle and suddenly yelped in pain, alerting the defenders of a Scottish castle. The thistle is used on the badges of many national and domestic sports teams.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Players">Players</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scotland_national_rugby_league_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Players">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Scotland_national_rugby_league_team_players" title="List of Scotland national rugby league team players">List of Scotland national rugby league team players</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Current_squad">Current squad</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scotland_national_rugby_league_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Current squad">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The Scotland national team squad for the <a href="/wiki/2017_Rugby_League_World_Cup" title="2017 Rugby League World Cup">2017 Rugby League World Cup</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Ryan_Brierley" title="Ryan Brierley">Ryan Brierley</a> was originally selected to play but withdrew due to injury. He was replaced by <a href="/wiki/Will_Oakes" title="Will Oakes">Will Oakes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<table class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scotland_national_rugby_league_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Player of the Year">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Since 2004, the Scottish management team have given the Dave Valentine Award to their player of the year.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> The award uses a voting system and is given to the player in early January.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a title="Huddersfield Giants">Huddersfield Giants</a>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Competitive_Record">Competitive Record</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scotland_national_rugby_league_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Competitive Record">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Scotland_national_rugby_league_team_match_results" title="Scotland national rugby league team match results">Scotland national rugby league team match results</a></div>\n<p>In 22 years of international rugby league Scotland have played 51 matches, winning 37% of them. Their most regular opponent has been Ireland, who similarly starting playing Rugby League in the mid-1990s.  In 1995, the <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain_national_rugby_league_team" title="Great Britain national rugby league team">Great Britain</a> team split into the separate home nations. This means that Scotland only started playing rugby league as an individual nation at this time and played their first ever game against <a href="/wiki/Ireland_national_rugby_league_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Ireland national rugby league team">Ireland</a> at <a href="/wiki/RDS_Arena" title="RDS Arena">RDS Arena</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dublin" title="Dublin">Dublin</a>.  The Irish won by a close score of 26\xe2\x80\x9322 in front of 5,716 fans.  Scotland have gone on to play Ireland the most times with 13 games, winning only four of these games.\n</p><p>Scotland have played <a href="/wiki/France_national_rugby_league_team" title="France national rugby league team">France</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wales_national_rugby_league_team" title="Wales national rugby league team">Wales</a> 10 and 9 times respectively.  Along with Ireland, these are the only teams that Scotland play on a regular basis.  Despite playing these home nations a number of times, they have only played <a href="/wiki/England_national_rugby_league_team" title="England national rugby league team">England</a> on one occasion, although they have also played England\'s 2nd team, \'the Knights\', once.  Scotland have played 13 other teams in their history but have not played more than 2 games against any of them.  Scotland have a 100% win record against 5 of these 12 teams and 0% record against 6.  In 22 years, they have only drawn 2 games, a 30\xe2\x80\x9330 result against <a href="/wiki/Italy_national_rugby_league_team" title="Italy national rugby league team">Italy</a> during the <a href="/wiki/2013_Rugby_League_World_Cup" title="2013 Rugby League World Cup">2013 Rugby League World Cup</a>, having previously beat them in their previous encounter by an incredible score of 104\xe2\x80\x930, also Scotland\'s record win and a 18-18 result against <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand_national_rugby_league_team" title="New Zealand national rugby league team">New Zealand</a> during the <a href="/wiki/2016_Rugby_League_Four_Nations" title="2016 Rugby League Four Nations">2016 Four Nations</a>; this result was considered one of the greatest results in international rugby league history and ensured that Scotland became the only \'fourth\' nation in Four Nations history to not be defeated by another team.\n</p><p>Scotland\'s highest home attendance is just 2,233.  This game was only their second and saw them defeated 22\xe2\x80\x9320 by <a href="/wiki/France_national_rugby_league_team" title="France national rugby league team">France</a> at <a href="/wiki/Firhill_Park" class="mw-redirect" title="Firhill Park">Firhill Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Glasgow" title="Glasgow">Glasgow</a>.  Rugby league is not a major sport in Scotland and home attendances average at around just 1,000.   Scotland\'s highest away attendance was much more when a crowd of 21,009 saw them defeated by 38\xe2\x80\x9312 against <a href="/wiki/England_national_rugby_league_team" title="England national rugby league team">England</a> during the 2016 Four Nations, this game being held at <a href="/wiki/Ricoh_Arena" title="Ricoh Arena">Ricoh Arena</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coventry" title="Coventry">Coventry</a>.\n</p>\n<table class="sortable wikitable">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Against\n</th>\n<th>Played\n</th>\n<th>Won\n</th>\n<th>Drawn\n</th>\n<th>Lost\n</th>\n<th>% class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scotland_national_rugby_league_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Four Nations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Scotland have only qualified for one Four Nations tournament where they made history by becoming the first fourth nation to earn a point after an 18-18 draw against New Zealand.\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable" style="text-align: center;">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th colspan="9"><a href="/wiki/Rugby_League_Four_Nations" class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scotland_national_rugby_league_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Support">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:ScotlandRLMerchandise.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/ScotlandRLMerchandise.jpg/220px-ScotlandRLMerchandise.jpg" width="220" height="197" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/ScotlandRLMerchandise.jpg/330px-ScotlandRLMerchandise.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/c8/ScotlandRLMerchandise.jpg 2x" data-file-width="412" data-file-height="369" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:ScotlandRLMerchandise.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>World Cup merchandise for fans.</div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Scotland" title="Sport in Scotland">Sport in Scotland</a></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Rugby_league_in_Scotland" title="Rugby league in Scotland">Rugby league in Scotland</a></div>\n<p>Rugby League is a minor sport in Scotland, with the country never having had a professional club.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> Participation in rugby league has increased though, with a Scottish division in the Rugby League Conference with seven teams,<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> including four in the Glasgow/West Scotland area<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> having formed in 2006. But, unlike in England, rugby league is not one of the ten most played sports in Scotland amongst adults.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> Junior development has been much more rapid, with several Conference teams having junior squads as well as other clubs who don\'t run an open-age squad having various junior squads. An estimated 2,500 children play rugby league in Scotland,<sup id="cite_ref-HNB_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HNB-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> with that figure growing to 12,500 when you add the amount of children who play the sport in various school programmes.<sup id="cite_ref-HNB_126-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HNB-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> In terms of media coverage, apart from <a href="/wiki/Challenge_Cup" title="Challenge Cup">Challenge Cup</a> matches rugby league is not shown on Scottish <a href="/wiki/Terrestrial_television" title="Terrestrial television">terrestrial television</a> and no matches are usually broadcast on radio. However, Scotland international matches usually get reported in national newspapers like <a href="/wiki/The_Scotsman" title="The Scotsman">The Scotsman</a> and sometimes in Scottish editions of London-based newspapers.\n</p><p>In 2009, the <a href="/wiki/Magic_Weekend" title="Magic Weekend">Magic Weekend</a>  was held at <a href="/wiki/Murrayfield_Stadium" title="Murrayfield Stadium">Murrayfield</a> with a two-day attendance of 60,000 spectators, including ticket sales of just under 7,000 in Scotland alone, making the event a success.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Statistics">Statistics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a
